# 太上助国救民总真秘要

**The Supreme Essential Secrets of the Dao for Assisting the State and Saving the People**

**Title:** *The Supreme Essential Secrets of the Dao for Assisting the State and Saving the People*
Compiled by Song Yuanmiaozong. Ten scrolls.
Source edition: *Zhengtong Daoist Canon*, Orthodox Section, Part One.

**Table of Contents**
Preface
Scroll 1: Preface to the *Orthodox Northern Dipper Celestial Heart Rites of Supreme Clarity*, along with the Petition Formats for the Exorcism Institute’s Practices and Regulations
Scroll 2: *Orthodox Northern Dipper Celestial Heart Rites of Supreme Clarity*—Divine Talismans and Incantations of the Dipper
Scroll 3: Talismanic Formulas for Dispelling Consumptive Illnesses and Miscellaneous Diseases, along with the *Authentic Rites of the Heavenly Vanguard for Expelling Demonic Influences*
Scroll 4: *Hidden Writings of Supreme Clarity: The Marrow of Divine Scriptures*, Part One
Scroll 5: *Hidden Writings of Supreme Clarity: The Marrow of Divine Scriptures*, Part Two
Scroll 6: *Hidden Writings of Supreme Clarity: The Marrow of Divine Scriptures*—*Demon Statutes and Jade Regulations of Ritual Forms*, Part Three
Scroll 7: Methods for Assisting the Righteous and Expelling the Demonic: Summoning and Examination Rites
Scroll 8: *The Supreme Orthodox Rites of Yu’s Paces*—Charts, Formulas, and Texts of the Dipper’s Guidance and Daily Palm Techniques
Scroll 9: Transmission and Ordination: Establishing the Earth Prison, Ascending the Terrace of Heavenly Birth—Divination Methods and Formulas for Dipper Lamps
Scroll 10: Official Document Formats for the *Northern Dipper Exorcism Institute’s* Dispatches

**Preface to *The Supreme Essential Secrets of the Dao for Assisting the State and Saving the People***

Your servant humbly observes: The Most High initiated transformation, deploying true *qi* to nurture all living beings. The Orthodox Unity transmitted its lineage, elucidating awe-inspiring majesty to reveal the hidden and the bound. Thus, divine scriptures and wondrous canons, though timely in their emergence, must align with the moment. The primordial statutes and true regulations truly serve as warnings against reckless transmission.

With reverence, I acknowledge the benevolent sagacity of the sovereign above, who has received the Heavenly Mandate, propagated the supreme Dao, and achieved perfection. Recently, a Palace of Precious Registers was established in the capital, and an ordination altar was set near the imperial precincts. Through talismanic remedies and healing elixirs, the well-being of the common people is safeguarded. Those who receive profound blessings number in the thousands daily, while those who turn toward the true wind account for eight or nine out of ten.

I have gathered and sought out immortal scriptures, mending omissions and completing lacunae. From all corners of the realm, nothing has been left uncollected. Now, I have compiled and collated these secret treasures, intending to engrave and transmit them for eternity, that the world may be steeped in primordial purity and the people may cultivate their nature and destiny. This may indeed be called an era of pure and complete *Dao*-*qi*, an age of ten thousand generations of Great Peace.

Your servant, by early fortune, has been graced with this opportunity, humbly dwelling among the feathered ranks. I have traversed the renowned mountains and sacred peaks of the four directions, seeking out masters and their teachings. For over thirty years, I have roughly grasped the essentials, preparing them for practical application. How could I not be stirred to action in such a time?

Formerly, while residing in Nanyang, I once used talismanic waters to relieve the suffering of the afflicted. Within a few years, the number of officials and commoners who benefited was beyond counting. One day, I was unexpectedly honored with an imperial decree...

Having been summoned to the palace gates, I was further honored with imperial titles and bestowed with gracious favors—how could my meager merits ever repay such celestial benevolence?

In the seventh month of the previous year, I was commissioned by decree to join the Scriptural Bureau, where I was tasked with collating lost texts and examining the *Qiongwen* Daoist Canon, as well as overseeing the carving of talismanic script. Through this, I was privileged to peruse the catalogues of scriptures. Among the vast array of divine chapters and precious talismans, nothing was lacking—yet I found the methods of healing the world and curing ailments, those arts timely and applicable for the present age, to be notably obscure and incomplete, without any comprehensive and readily usable texts.

Unwilling to hoard what I have learned, and undeterred by my own inadequacies, I have compiled the talismanic methods and secret oral instructions I received into ten scrolls, entitled *The Supreme Essential Secrets for Assisting the Nation and Saving the People*. Having transcribed this work in full, I now humbly present it, hoping it may modestly aid the sagely intent, uncover even a fraction of the Dao’s manifold teachings, and serve future disciples by broadening their knowledge. This is the deepest aspiration of this unworthy servant in the Way.

Composed with reverence on the fifteenth day of the intercalary first month of the sixth year of the Zhenghe era.

By *Dongyou* Master Yuan Miaozong.

*Scroll One of The Supreme Essential Secrets for Assisting the Nation and Saving the People*
Compiled by Yuan Miaozong, Master of Mysteries.

*Preface to the Supreme Clarity Northern Culmen Heavenly Heart Orthodox Methods, with the Petition and Protocol for the Bureau of Expelling Malevolence*

I have heard that the Heavenly Heart Methods are the methods of the Northern Culmen and Central Dipper. The Northern Culmen is the central pole of Heaven, where all phenomena converge. The Northern Dipper is the central Dipper of Heaven, from which all qi is bestowed. Thus, as the heart of Heaven, these methods originate therefrom, sharing their lineage with the Orthodox Unity tradition and serving as the pivotal mechanism for exorcism and governance.

Since ancient times, Master Rao Jun’s *Register of Hidden Merits* has been revered in celestial intent, with divine talismans conferred and secret oral instructions received upon the Purple Empyrean. The transmission of these methods has been passed down through successive lineages, thereby illuminating them for the world. Whether for summoning blessings, dispelling malevolence, discerning the principles of yin and yang, or distinguishing the affairs of the unseen and manifest realms, no matter is left unaddressed. The methods are concise in application, and none surpass these in efficacy.

In recent times, scholars of lofty conduct, aiding Heaven’s transformative work and assisting the nation to save the people, have particularly esteemed these methods. Yet in their application, some have found their efficacy lacking. This is due to transmissions that fail in profound erudition, studies that do not delve deeply into the ultimate techniques, Dao-powers that remain incomplete, and divine marvels that are scarcely prepared. Merely entangled in names and forms, how can such efforts yield benefit?

I have therefore meticulously compiled the foundational methods along with their secret oral instructions, gathering talismans and seals, outlining the steps for pacing the Dipper’s network, and exhaustively elucidating the essentials of its peripheral connections and hidden mysteries. Obscure principles are clarified, and extant texts are briefly expounded, valuing practice and conveying the subtleties of the primordial and wondrous. May this work, in its dissemination, serve as an inexhaustible ford for those who traverse it.

According to the statutes, the Heavenly Heart Orthodox Methods and the Supreme Clarity secret instructions require, for all transmissions, adherence to the prescribed time limits, declaration of the ritual protocols, and verification of the responses from the true and numinous. Only then may they be applied; unauthorized transmission is strictly forbidden. Violations of these prohibitions will not only render the divine qi ineffectual but also incur penalties from both the unseen and manifest realms, with calamities that are by no means light.

The protocols for transmission and ordination are set forth in the subsequent scrolls. Scholars should examine these with care.

*Prayers, Supplications, and Exorcisms*

When a nation prays for rain, whether enduring prolonged drought or suffering from locusts and pestilence that harm the people, or when baleful stars align with its astrological regions, or when border raiders invade its territory and enemy forces press near, or when flood dragons and water spirits capsize boats and sweep away lives—such matters, great or small, all require urgent memorials to Heaven, petitioning the Heavenly Hosts for extermination, and submitting writs to the celestial star palaces, the Five Peaks, the Four Watercourses, the Four Seas, the Nine Rivers, and the dragon deities. Dispatches must also be sent to the local city gods, the spirits of mountains, rivers, and roads governing the affected regions, as well as to the Six Dings, Six Jias, and the Cloud and Thunder Departments. The presiding spirit-officials must be duly appointed, or if commoners submit petitions, they shall declare that within such-and-such a domain, for such-and-such a matter, a ritual platform has been established at such-and-such a place, with the altar prepared in reverent anticipation. Once the response is manifest, a grand jiao offering shall be conducted to express gratitude for Heaven’s grace. The memorial shall record the dispatched officers and soldiers, who upon their return shall be rewarded with promotions and ranks as proof of efficacy. The rituals must be performed with utmost sincerity to ensure a clear and potent response; negligence or laxity will result in impeachment by the Four Offices, scrutiny by the Three Officials, and punishment for violating Heaven’s statutes—a crime that admits no pardon.

**Treating Madness and Malevolent Spirits**
To treat afflictions caused by madness or malevolent spirits, first obtain a sworn statement from the afflicted detailing the circumstances. Based on the nature of the case, determine the appropriate authorities to petition. Begin by issuing a writ to the afflicted’s household Controller of Destiny and the Five Paths Earth God, then dispatch a memorial to the local prefectural or county city god. Alternatively, petition the relevant celestial battalion to capture the spirit, or memorialize Heaven to establish a celestial prison for its confinement. All official documents and dispatched troops must first be accompanied by offerings; only then shall writs, passes, and summons be issued for execution. Next, provide the afflicted with talismanic water for ingestion and wearing. After the grace is received, reward the soldiers again and conduct a vegetarian feast or jiao offering to thank Heaven for its divine favor. The scale of the jiao offering should be commensurate with the family’s wealth—modest for the poor, lavish for the rich. If the family is truly impoverished and unable to prepare the offerings, the master shall provide them on their behalf. Should the wealthy, after receiving grace, begrudge their wealth and fail to offer thanks, thus dishonoring the soldiers’ merit, they shall incur misfortune that cannot be exorcised or resolved.

**Mountain Imps and Spectral Beings**
Mountain imps are unorthodox spirits of the Five Phases, falsely claiming to be sages, seducing women, stirring waters, setting fires, hurling bricks and stones, tormenting livestock, manifesting eerie lights, assuming living forms, roaming day and night, and terrifying people—all manner of strange phenomena. First, examine the petition to assess the severity of the harm. For cases of grave concern, follow the above procedures: urgently memorialize Heaven and petition the relevant sacred peak for troops, or dispatch a writ to the local city god. The methods employed—including rewards—shall adhere to the preceding examples.

**Transmission of Corpse Qi and Recurring Afflictions**

To sever the transmission of corpse qi and recurring afflictions, and to dissolve curses and maledictions, first obtain a written statement from the afflicted. It should state: the illness suffered by the person, the names of family members who previously died of the same illness on such-and-such a year, month, and day, or how many others later perished from it—all deceased must be listed by name. If the family has performed any meritorious deeds or held memorial rites that have not yet yielded results, immediately submit an urgent memorial to Heaven and petition the Eastern Peak, requesting a writ be sent to the Earth Prison to grant leave for messengers to escort the deceased to the Terrace of Heavenly Ascent, where their traces may be revealed and they may receive the scriptures and methods.

Conduct a Yellow Register Daoist ritual for several days and nights. Bathe, prepare paper garments, set out offerings, and receive the precepts. Burn the talismans of the Dragon Youth and transmit the True Talisman of the Most High for Salvation from Suffering. Present memorials and petitions, listing the names of the deceased for deliverance. Upon completion of the fast, dispatch the Four Upright Messengers with the fast’s certificate and the altar’s writ to escort the deceased to the Earth Prison, where they shall meet with the Merit Bureau and the officials of the Heavenly Ascent Case to receive rebirth according to the established rites.

After rewarding the troops, perform the *Xiagai* Rite to permanently sever future afflictions, and provide the afflicted with talismanic water to swallow and wear. If the deceased frequently appear in dreams to cause harm, possessing the living and explaining matters, and if they are not external ghosts, then meritorious deeds must be performed to assist their ascent to the realm of the living.

For cases where the haunting is caused by deceased senior relatives or close kin, perform memorial rites to ensure mutual deliverance for the living and the dead, preventing further harm. Upon resolution, reward the troops as in the preceding examples.

For curses and maledictions that have caused death, perform meritorious deeds commensurate with the family’s wealth. After redemption is complete, submit a memorial to halt the curses permanently. Do not invoke the talismanic shrines; ensure the curses are severed for all time.

**Dispelling Epidemics**

To expel the ghostly legions of pestilence—afflictions such as febrile illnesses, heat diseases, smallpox, red eyes, mouth sores, the five types of malaria, alternating chills and fever, madness, diarrhea, and dysentery—where medicine has failed and prayers have gone unanswered: first obtain a truthful statement from the afflicted and submit it to the relevant authorities, or urgently memorialize Heaven. Command the performance of a jiao offering to repent and expiate transgressions before providing talismanic water to swallow and wear.

Issue a writ to the Twelve Year-Kings to restrain the advance of the epidemic, preventing the spread of poisonous drugs and toxic qi. Seal the household with a protective talisman and perform the *Xiagai* Rite to ensure the family is forever free from pestilence. Reward the troops and send off the ghostly legions of pestilence to distant lands. On the day the crisis is resolved, hold a jiao offering to thank Heaven for its grace and protection.

**Praying for Offspring**

**Praying for Offspring**

When a couple has been married for many years without bearing sons or daughters, or when children die in infancy, or when only daughters are born and no sons, or when young children perish prematurely—this may be due to the mutual affliction of the Six Harms, encountering solitary stars or barren constellations, or the accumulation of past misdeeds making it difficult to continue the lineage. In such cases, the birth years, months, days, and hours of the husband and wife must be recorded and urgently memorialized to Heaven, while also submitting a petition to the Register of Births and the Eastern Peak. A special request shall be made to bestow a son upon the petitioner. Talismans shall be issued for swallowing and wearing, and the couple must be instructed to perform meritorious deeds in advance, such as commissioning sacred images, and await the response of divine grace. Once the blessing is received, a vegetarian feast and jiao offering shall be held to thank the Perfected Ones for their benevolence.

**Expiating Disasters and Illnesses**

To expiate disasters and repent of transgressions: when years of calamity and suffering confine one to bed, when medicine and food fail to cure, when prayers go unanswered—this may be due to the influence of stars and planets, the harm of vengeful spirits, violations of earthly taboos, or the karmic retribution of past deeds in this life, provoking Heaven’s censure and the false accusations of ghosts below. For those seeking expiation, repentance must come first. Hold a vegetarian feast, perform a jiao offering, present memorials, and submit petitions, hoping that the sagely Dao will take pity and absolve their faults. Only then may the crisis be resolved.

**Destroying Unorthodox Shrines**

To destroy unorthodox shrines: these refer to deities not recognized in the state’s sacrificial canon, those who cling to trees and grass or lurk in springs and pools—wild specters and mountain spirits that harm people and things, demanding bloody sacrifices, spreading illness, and bringing every kind of misfortune. If complaints are filed, a petition shall be submitted to the Eastern Peak and urgently memorialized to Heaven, dispatching heavenly soldiers to capture and punish these deceitful and disorderly spirits. Their shrines shall be burned, and they shall be tried according to the law. If a private shrine, sustained by incense offerings, brings blessings to the local people, a petition with the testimony of community elders and neighbors shall be submitted to Heaven, requesting permission to rebuild the shrine and allow the people to continue their worship.

According to the statutes on governing ghosts, official temples dedicated to deities in the state’s sacrificial canon must not be used to solicit private offerings, secretly accept bloody sacrifices, or permit curses that wrongfully seize living souls, imprisoning them and driving people to drown themselves, leap into fires, or inflict self-harm, abandoning their livelihoods and stirring up lawsuits. For all illnesses, misfortunes, and losses of family wealth, complaints may be filed with detailed accounts, and once verified, petitions shall be submitted to await divine response and enforcement. If living people have inadvertently offended the principles of the gods, bringing misfortune upon themselves, they may confess and make amends, but the gods must not harm the lives of the people. Even if offenses are grave, repentance shall still be permitted.

**Miscellaneous Malevolent Qi and Other Matters**

When ghosts and various malevolent entities spread pernicious qi, spoiling wine and vinegar, or when taboos are violated, causing household unrest; when ancient tombs are excavated and buried corpses cause harm; when livestock behave strangely, devouring their own young; when insects and rats cry out unnaturally, hens crow at night, or snakes and ants release venom into homes; when knives, spears, rods, and swords make phantom noises; when ghosts appear at night, filling the heart with terror; when spirits open and close doors, strike objects, arrange cups and utensils for feasts, or drive people to throw themselves into wells or hang themselves; when they make people weep or sing, or fill them with sorrow and discontent; when they dissipate family wealth, borrow others’ clothes, or set fires to burn homes; when they call out people’s names, or malevolent qi enters their hearts and bellies, causing nightmares, ghostly apparitions, and sleep disturbances; when they provoke lawsuits and disputes, discord between husband and wife, or difficult childbirth; when they ruin fields and silkworms, prevent crops from flourishing, cause merchants to suffer losses, or obstruct all endeavors; when ghosts and spirits gather in new homes, whirlwinds enter dwellings, foxes cry out in confusion, or large trees fall without wind; when cauldrons wail and overflow, household objects move on their own, or infants cry at night, disrupting the harmony of men and women; when servants flee, livestock die of plague, or ghosts appear in broad daylight, manifesting in eerie sounds, lights, and illusions—these myriad demonic harms and destructive forces are too numerous to recount in full.

Here, a few examples are given so that it may be known that the law contains statutes to subdue them. No matter how great or small the matter, there are regulations to address it. However, if the handling of such cases lacks evidence and verges on deception, they shall not fall within the scope of enforcement. After receiving divine grace, the rites of rewarding the troops and offering thanks must be performed according to one’s means, and the rituals must not be entirely neglected.

The gods are not distant; they are before our very eyes and ears. If one fails to believe and instead mocks or profanes them, the sins will extend to past generations, the calamities will befall descendants, and disasters will arise swiftly—by then, regret will be too late.

The above excerpts from the statutes of the law are compiled into these several sections, clearly categorized and explained, easy to understand. They are illustrated and made known to the people. Those who suffer and seek remedy shall follow them without doubt. Those who disbelieve and profane them shall study and reflect, that they may come to repent.

Here the Dao acts as Heaven’s deputy to succor all beings—demands for wealth or property must not be made lightly. Should any petition for life or submit in sincerity, the statutes and ordinances must never be slighted or delayed. All who come to this court to file petitions or request talismanic water shall thoroughly study and understand these instructions.

*Tai Shang Zhu Guo Jiu Min Zong Zhen Mi Yao*, Scroll One (end)
[Note: The character *ze* 責 was originally written as *gui* 貴; emended here according to context.]

*Tai Shang Zhu Guo Jiu Min Zong Zhen Mi Yao*, Scroll Two
Compiled by Dongyou Master Yuan Miaozong of the Supreme Purity Northern Culmen Heavenly Heart Orthodox Rites, under the Dipper’s Numinous Writs and Incantations

**Essential Methods for Preserving Stability and Dispensing Cures**
For averting epidemics, treating critical illnesses, severing consumptive *qi* transmission, subduing frenzied or demonic spirits, and dismantling improper talismanic shrines: first purify oneself, light incense, complete the pacing of the stellar net, transform into the divine form, and silently offer reverent invocation to the Supreme Purity Northern Culmen Great Emperor. Then pace the Dipper’s net, recite the Dipper incantation, and upon reaching *Po Jun* (Breaking Army), recite the *Celestial Net Great Sage Incantation*. After releasing the Dipper mudra, proceed with the *Heavenly Marshal Mudra*.

Next, face the Four Seasonal Palaces to pay homage to the Jade Emperor. Record the circumstances and abridge the details, then submit the memorial according to protocol and await the Jade Emperor’s decree. Proceed to the afflicted household, dispatching two divine generals to follow. At the household’s gate, invoke the divine transformation phrase to summon the generals, employing both the *Celestial Emperor Mudra* and *Heavenly Marshal Mudra*. Envision the petitioner as the *Four Upright Merit Officers* and the *Generals of the Six Ding and Six Jia*, accompanied by the local earth deity. Then select and activate the necessary mudras for the task at hand.

**Dipper’s Seven Stars Method for Dispelling Malevolence**
Envision the Northern Dipper’s stars overarching and pressing down upon one’s head, the net’s handle pointing forward. Imagine the arms, elbows, and chest forming a Dipper constellation. Then pace the Northern Dipper’s Seven Kings into the household, beginning with *Tan Lang* (Greedy Wolf), the net’s handle pointing ahead. Proceed to the main hall and take a seat.

Envision oneself as the Envoy of the Northern Culmen Demon-Quelling Court, the left hand holding the *Seal of the Great Dharma Master of All Heavens*, the right hand wielding the *Samadhi Fire Bell Sword*, clad in the regalia of the *Three Heavens Orthodox Unity Perfected*: the *Jiaotai* crown, fish-scale robe, and vermilion shoes with raven talons. To the left and right, envision the *Four Heavenly Kings*, the *Eight Great Vajras*, the *Twelve Great Spirits* of the twelve earthly branches, the *Generals of the Six Ding and Six Jia*, the *Two Merit Officers* of the current day and hour, and the *Earth Deity* of the locale. Then proceed with the matter according to the prescribed method.

**Divine Transformation Mudra**
For all rites of dispatch and command, first perform the divine transformation: press the *Root Master Mudra*, envisioning oneself as the Envoy of the Demon-Quelling Court, clad in the Celestial Master’s regalia. The two divine generals and the day-and-hour merit officers stand to the left and right. Then employ the *Celestial Emperor Mudra*.

Next, perform the *Divine Transformation Mudra* and recite the incantation. For dispatch, press the *Celestial Emperor Mudra* with both hands, clicking the teeth thirty-six times. Then pace the stellar net as usual, softly intoning:

*"The disciple of the Tai Shang’s register of rites, [Name and Rank], respectfully summons the Year Spirit, the Monthly General, and the officers and soldiers of the Six Jia. At this day and hour, the divine generals of the register’s direct talisman, the thousand-strong army of Dharma-assisting generals, and the cavalry of the Six Ding officers of the day—all descend together. The marching spirits deploy their *qi*."*

Click the teeth seven times, then recite:
*"Seal the Divine Transformation Mudra and intone the Divine Transformation Incantation:*
*I am no mortal form—*
*My head resembles dark clouds,*
*My hair like scattered stars.*
*My left eye is the sun,*
*My right eye the moon.*
*My nose is a fire bell,*
*My ears golden chimes.*
*My upper lip is the Rain Master,*
*My lower lip the Wind Earl.*
*My teeth are a forest of swords,*
*My ten fingers like merit officers.*
*I command the Lord of Min Mountain to my left flank,*
*The Lord of Lu Mountain to my right flank.*
*I command the Thunder General of the Left to my left foot,*
*The Lightning General of the Right to my right foot.*
*I command the Lord of Mount Tai to my spine.*
*The Thirty-Six Beasts and Twenty-Eight Constellations—*
*All respond to my body.*
*Hasten, hasten, as the statutes command!"*

**Recognizing the Sacred Images of the Rites**
*The Northern Culmen Five Numinous Elder Lord*: Radiant in a dark crown and feathered robes, resembling the full moon’s orb, within which appears an emperor, faintly flanked by jade maidens. His retinue resembles the imperial household, with the emperor’s tabooed name clearly discernible.

*The Upper Terrace Perfected Lord*: Ten feet tall, his face golden, exhaling yellow *qi* that suffuses the world. His hair unbound in Daoist attire, clad in pale yellow robes, holding a jade scepter. He rides a triad of subtle, dark clouds, a yellow *qi* emanating from his crown. His name: *Xu Jing*.

*The Middle Terrace Perfected Lord*: Ten feet tall, his face luminous white, exhaling white *qi* that fills the world. Clad in white Daoist robes, holding a white scepter. He rides white clouds, a white *qi* emanating from his crown. His name: *Liu Chun*.

*The Lower Terrace Perfected Lord*: Ten feet tall, his face azure with radiant beams, his *qi* like threads piercing the darkness to form a halo of blue-green *qi*. Clad in azure Daoist robes, holding a green scepter. His name: *Qu Chun*.

*The Star Lord Tan Lang*: Twelve feet tall, resembling a wild ghostly marshal, his hair unbound, his complexion greenish-red. His left hand leans on a white staff, his right hand rests on his front.

*The Star Lord Ju Men*: Resembling a beautiful woman, adorned with tassels and filigree, wearing a five-colored floral crown, holding a luminous precious fan. Attended by azure-clad maidens.

*The Star Lord Lu Cun*: Resembling a handsome man of twenty, his face florid, clad in grass garments, holding paper and brush, standing squarely.

*The Star Lord Wen Qu*: His hair unbound, holding texts, riding a five-colored cloud dragon, his countenance like a woman’s.

*The Star Lord Lian Zhen*: Hair bound in a single topknot, riding a white dragon, wearing a seven-jeweled crown. Four attendants, each wielding a halberd, follow *Wu Qu*.

*The Star Lord Wu Qu*: Elephant-headed with a human face, wielding a sword, adorned with tassels and filigree. Four attendants, each wielding a halberd, follow.

*The Star Lord Po Jun*: Boar-headed with a human face, holding a *huān xǐ tuán* (joyous orb), clad in plain white robes, his mouth exhaling red *qi* that outshines the sun, standing at the Dipper’s handle.

*The Auxiliary Star*: Crowned and robed, holding a tablet, clad in the attire of a worldly chief minister.

The Seven Primordial Star Lords: All clad in Daoist yellow robes, riding yellow clouds, holding white jade tablets, with dark *qi* emanating from their crowns.

The Auxiliary Star: In crimson robes, like the Seven Stars. Standing ten feet tall, holding a jade tablet, exhaling clouds of five-colored *qi*.

The Heavenly Valiant Great Sage Emperor, enfeoffed as the Vajra King and leader of the Seven Primordials: A hundred feet tall, wearing plain silk, hair unbound, left hand on hip, right hand wielding a sword, standing with feet apart. From his crown issue two streams of *qi*—one blue, one white—within which red *qi* threads appear, to be gathered by incantation.

Zhenwu: A hundred feet tall, hair unbound, clad in golden interlocking armor. His feet rest upon the Five-Colored Spirit Tortoise, also called the Tortoise of the *Tengshe* and Eight Trigrams. Hand on sword, eyes blazing like lightning. When employing Zhenwu talismans, one draws his *qi* to empower the ink in the brush and inkstone, then writes with the Dipper mudra.

Nine attendants, each holding banners and halberds, accompany him on black clouds.

The Heavenly *Ding* Valiant Warriors: Crimson robes with wide sleeves, wearing ceremonial caps and holding halberds. Surnamed *Gou*, named *Minzi*.

The Divine Generals: Black robes with crimson headbands, appearing as divine beings. Leading troops, wielding swords, assisting in rituals with halberds, or assuming the guise of generals.

The master’s incantation invokes them thus:
*"The Northern Emperor’s Generals, charged with expelling evil.
Vast in divine power, with claws and fangs long.
Their might shakes heaven and earth, their *qi* like clouds and mist.
Leading officials and soldiers, commanding yakshas.
Behind, swords and halberds follow; ahead, thunder chariots race.
Their awe strikes the earth, raising dust to the right.
Rewarding the upright, capturing malevolent spirits.
All ghosts who bring harm shall be seized without exception.
Hasten! As the law commands."*

The general emerges to the left.

*"The Northern Emperor’s Generals, charged with dispelling pestilence.
Above, they receive the sacred decree; below, they save the people.
Their virtue aligns with heaven and earth, their might shakes the cosmos.
Feet treading the vast sea, heads crowned by Kunlun.
Behind, valiant warriors follow; ahead, three armies advance.
Driving thunder and fire, swords and halberds like clouds.
Clearing paths for humanity, blocking the gates of ghosts.
By night, they slay evil ghosts; by day, they devour the Five Pestilences.
All calamitous spirits are seized and brought before the Emperor.
Severed without mercy, crushed to dust.
Hasten! As the law commands."*

The general emerges to the right.

The Functionaries: Crowned, wearing vermilion shoes, wielding swords. Invoked by the master’s incantation according to the day and hour.

The Earth Deity: In a white ceremonial robe, wrapped in a headcloth, wearing boots, standing three feet and two inches tall. Invoked by the master’s incantation.

The Day Officers:
- *Zi* Day Officer: Rat-headed with a human body, in black robes, holding a spear.
- *Chou* Day Officer: Ox-headed with a human body, in yellow robes, holding the same.
- *Yin* Day Officer: Tiger-headed with a human body, in green robes, holding a *jian* (a halberd with a red tassel).
- *Mao* Day Officer: Rabbit-headed with a human body, in green robes, holding a *jian*.
- *Chen* Day Officer: Dragon-headed with a human body, in yellow robes, holding a *jian*.
- *Si* Day Officer: Snake-headed with a human body, in red robes, holding a halberd with a cord.
- *Wu* Day Officer: Horse-headed with a human body, in red robes, holding a halberd.
- *Wei* Day Officer: Goat-headed with a human body, in yellow robes, holding a halberd.
- *Shen* Day Officer: Monkey-headed with a human body, in white robes, holding a spear.
- *You* Day Officer: Rooster-headed with a human body, in white robes, holding a spear.
- *Xu* Day Officer: Dog-headed with a human body, in yellow robes, holding a spear.
- *Hai* Day Officer: Pig-headed with a human body, in black robes, holding a spear.

The above Day Officers, along with mountain soldiers and fierce ghostly warriors, wear armor and wield halberds.

The Heavenly Realm Day Officer: *Jiao Gongnu*.
The Earthly Realm Day Officer: *Zheng Yuanxi*.
The Void Realm Day Officer: *Zhang Yuanbo*.

The Director of the Expelling-Evil Bureau: Celestial Master Zhang. Clad in a white fish-scale robe, wearing a *Jiaotai* crown and vermilion shoes. In his left hand, he holds the Seal of the Lord of the Great Dao; in his right, the Sword of the Northern Dipper and the Fire Bell of *Samadhi*.

The Instructors:
- Instructor *Tan*: Crane-bodied with a pine-like form, wearing a *Huayang* cap and a purple crane-feather cloak, styled *Lingxu*.
- Instructor *Rao*: With refined brows and eyes, standing over five feet tall, dignified and elegant. Clad in a crane-feather cloak and a *Huayang* cap.

A Divine General dispatched by the Eastern Peak to reinforce the troops: Wearing a *chaotian* headcloth, a black embroidered golden-flowered robe, a red silk headband, a jade belt, golden interlocking armor, and green-dragon-patterned boots. Twelve *zhang* tall, wielding a long steel sword, riding a red horse, bearing a red embroidered banner. He commands officials and soldiers, safeguarding the true Dao. When rescue is needed, or to capture demonic thieves and execute punishments, he transmits orders clearly, disciplines the troops, and ensures victory. Upon receiving commands, he acts immediately and reports back upon completion.

The Assistant Divine Generals: Holding yellow battle-axes, riding white horses, bearing yellow embroidered banners, clad in armor and robes like the Commanding General. United in purpose, they lead officials and soldiers to protect the ritual master. In rescue, capture, or punitive actions, they collaborate in strategy, transmit orders, discipline the troops, and ensure victory. Upon receiving commands, they act and report back.

Two Commanding Generals, ten Deputy Generals, twenty Company Commanders, five Dragon Spirits, five Sacred Peak Lords, and a thousand elite soldiers.

One Master of Ceremonies, two Registrars, twelve Bureau Officers, four Day Functionaries, and one Earth Deity.

The ten Deputy Generals: Of varying appearances, each ten feet tall, wearing helmets, golden armor, and holding bows, arrows, spears, and swords, each with five-colored banners, riding horses.

The two Commanding Generals lead their troops, surrounding and capturing enemies, executing punishments, and obeying the orders of the Commanding General to rally the ranks, ensuring might and valor.

Twenty Company Commanders, clad in silver helmets and interlocking armor, wielding sharp weapons. Each stands nine feet and five inches tall, sometimes mounted, sometimes on foot. They constantly assist the ten Deputy Generals in driving and commanding their units, shaking the earth with their might, responding swiftly to duties, and striving to achieve merit and accomplish tasks.

Five Dragon Spirits, corresponding to the five, are ever tasked with restraining and commanding the dragon deities to safeguard the Daoist arts. Should this court perform rites to pray for rain, aiding the state and benefiting the people, they lead and summon the dragons to ensure timely rainfall. If this court captures and executes malevolent spirits, they demolish lairs and temples, level mountains and marshes, sweep away evil spirits, and spread flourishing qi to subdue monsters and banish demons.

Two Valiant Guardsmen of the Left and Right, responsible for establishing the penal dungeons and personally providing protection. Nine Wardens of the Nine Prisons: when this court imprisons and interrogates spirits and deities, each leads their divine soldiers to ensure strict confinement, allowing no escape, manifestation of form, or revelation of sound or appearance. They promptly report and transfer the released prisoners to the appropriate authorities. Each must hold implements such as staffs, cangues, fetters, and whips for binding and punishment.

One thousand elite soldiers, each nine feet tall, dressed in multicolored garments, wearing bronze helmets and iron armor, each bearing weapons, bows, and swords. They are organized in units of five, with five units forming a squad, four squads under a Deputy General, and two squads under a Company Commander. All are heroic, brave, fierce, and agile, capturing demonic thieves and subduing malevolent spirits. Should evil ghosts or fiends dare to resist, they ready their weapons and exert all efforts to execute and slay them, striving to establish merit. The Deputy Generals and Company Commanders clearly instruct their units, ensuring no negligence or slackness.

One Master of Ceremonies at the Altar, wearing the ancient *dafu* cap, the ancient *dafu* robes, a sword, and holding a tablet, with ceremonial shoes. They inspect and discipline the generals, officers, and soldiers, ensuring strict order. They maintain constant vigilance in ceremonial propriety.

Should rescue or capture be required, the generals, officers, and soldiers are to be promptly assembled. Those with merit shall be rewarded, while offenders shall face no pardon.

One Registrar of the Military Bureau attends, with four Executive Officers, to maintain the rosters and numbers of the troops. For all generals, officers, and soldiers engaged in punitive expeditions, rescues, or healings, they record merits and transgressions, standardize reports, and submit them for strategic consideration. A Co-adjutant may be appointed to assist in deliberation and execution.

Eight Attendant Officers follow the commanding general, managing miscellaneous affairs. Some hold designated duties, while others serve without fixed posts, dispatched as needed to transmit orders. Four Timekeepers on duty, assigned by year, month, day, and hour, assist with elite troops. They ensure strict confidentiality in strategic matters, summon spirits, relay commands, receive and present documents, submit memorials, and handle official correspondence. They facilitate clear communication and responses without delay.

One Altar Earth Deity attends, overseeing the land wherever the Bureau travels, governing the spirits within its jurisdiction. Upon receiving directives from the Institute, they transmit orders, summon spirits to search for and apprehend malevolent entities, and relay official documents. The Bureau’s authority extends to isolating and suppressing evil persons, tigers, wolves, venomous snakes, defilements, inauspicious omens, lingering corpses, and pernicious *qi*, meticulously inspecting and eradicating them without fail.

One Supervisor of the Military Kitchen oversees the Institute’s food and provisions. For all banquets and meals, utmost care is taken to ensure purity and cleanliness, driving away rats, ants, flies, insects, cats, dogs, and all impurities. Should demonic thieves conceal themselves or commit defilement, they are to manifest divine might to instill fear and awe.

Each role bears its own responsibility, and thus none may be absent.

**Incantation for Dispatching the *Gongcao* Spirits**

Summon the *Gongcao* Attendant on duty this day, heed my words.
By decree of the Supreme Heaven, I assist in the Dao’s transformation, aid the state and save the people, cure illness and expel demons, sever evil and establish rectitude.
When I dispatch you to Heaven, go swiftly to the Celestial Bureau.
When I dispatch you to Earth, proceed directly to the Underworld.
When I dispatch you to Water, enter at once the Water Palace.
Within the Three Realms, all malevolent spirits and ghosts—regardless of rank—must be swiftly seized wherever they lurk.
I now cure illness and expel demons; delay not.
Receive this written command, dare not disobey, and carry it out with reverence.
*Hasten, hasten!* I await you before the altar, sword planted firm.

**Incantation for Dispatching the Local Earth Spirit**

Spirits of Heaven, spirits of Earth, where Heaven and Earth converge.
Receive this missive, Earth Spirit—tarry not.
Go swiftly, return swiftly; I await you before the altar, sword planted firm.

**Method for Inscribing Talismans**

Before inscribing a talisman, first notify the Attendant Spirits of the Three Realms, declaring the purpose of this summons.
May all the Great Saints within the talisman descend in majesty, infusing the brush with their radiance.
When inscribing talismans for others or practicing self-cultivation—whether pacing the stars or treading the Dipper—observe the yin-yang days. To disregard this is to render them feeble and ineffectual.

**Yang Days:** Jia, Bing, Wu, Geng, Ren.
**Yin Days:** Yi, Ding, Ji, Xin, Gui.

When inscribing talismans, employ the Dipper Mudra.
Trace the form of the Three Terraces, letting each star guide the brush, drawing *qi* to infuse the brush.
For the **Upper Terrace**, emit yellow *qi* from the crown.
For the **Middle Terrace**, emit white *qi* from the crown.
For the **Lower Terrace**, emit blue-green *qi* from the crown.

When inscribing talismans:
- For the Three Terraces, use the Three Terraces Incantation, writing the character *chi* (敕) in ink with the Jade Emperor Mudra.
- For the characters of the Sun, Moon, and the Great Sage of Heaven’s Might, write in cinnabar while reciting the Heavenly Emperor’s Mantra, completing the word as the incantation ends.
- For the Seven Stars, write in cinnabar while reciting the Dipper-Splitting Incantation.
- For the Great Sage of Black Killing, follow the preceding incantation and method.
- For the Three Clarities’ *chi* (敕), write in ink using the appropriate mudra.
- For the character *ni* (聻), recite the Heavenly Marshal Tianpeng’s Incantation and use the Tianpeng Mudra, completing the word as the incantation ends.
- For the character *sha* (煞), use the Shangqing Mudra.
- For the character *gui* (鬼), use the Dipper Mudra.
- For the Seven Bindings and Seven Killings, recite the incantations while visualizing the true *qi*.

When inscribing talismans or performing rituals, first calm the mind and banish all distracting thoughts.
Sit facing the direction of the day’s destruction.
Visualize your master before you, along with the master who transmitted the teachings, and your ancestral master behind you.

The Supreme Emperor of Highest Clarity, Ancestral Master, is attended by the thirty-six great generals of Heavenly Marshal Tianpeng and Heavenly Marshal Tianyou. Visualize yourself as the Envoy of the Demon-Quelling Court, assuming the form of the Heavenly Master—wearing the Dipper upon your head, your front foot treading upon the Stern Star, your rear foot upon the Chief Star. Draw the true *qi* of the Sun, Moon, and Heavenly Stern into your mouth, then exhale it in accordance with the method’s completion, proceeding step by step without error or disorder. This *qi*: the true *qi* of the Great Yang is fiery in hue; the true *qi* of the Great Yin is silvery; the true *qi* of the Heavenly Stern is crimson. When inscribing talismans and drawing *qi*, employ the preceding method.

The *qi* of the Three Lights and the Incantation for Consecrating the Brush:
**Incantation of the Seven Bindings of the Moon Sovereign**
*Oṃ vajra □ ra □ ra svāhā.*

**Incantation of the Seven Killings of the Sun Sovereign**
*Oṃ vajra □ ra guṇa-lī svāhā.*

**Incantation of the True *Qi* of the Heavenly Stern**
The Chapter of the Heavenly Emperor’s Release,
Adorned with the Heavenly Stern.
Why do the malevolent ghosts of the five directions not perish?
With a single inhalation of the Flying Immortal, ten thousand ghosts hide in submission.
Great Sage of the Heavenly Stern, seize the hearts of ghosts.

Recite the incantations of the Sun, Moon, and Heavenly Stern, drawing their true *qi* into the talisman.

**Incantation for Consecrating the Brush (with the Dipper Mudra)**
Great Sage of the Heavenly Stern,
Revered Star of the Northern Dipper.
Execute and slay the malevolent,
Eradicating traces and forms.
Demon kings tremble in fear,
Their gall shattered, their hearts overturned.
Deliver the people from suffering,
Bestow mighty numinous power.
Cure illness, dispel misfortune,
Reverse death into life.
Where the celestial talisman arrives,
Demonic spirits are severed.
Descend with true *qi*,
Divine might be enacted.
*Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!*

**Mudra of the Three Clarities’ *Chi***
*Chi* of the Jade Clarity,
*Chi* of the Highest Clarity—use the Three Clarities Mudra and flick.
*Chi* of the Grand Clarity—thereafter, draw again.

For driving away and annihilating fierce demons, violent ghosts, spectral winds, raging anomalies, malignant pestilence, and consumptive corpse-transmission, employ the Three Clarities’ *chi*. For minor matters, simply follow the usual form in inscribing.

The Dipper Star Form—assemble the shapes within the Three Terraces Star Diagram and inscribe in cinnabar.

Where the Four Heavens seal black turbid *qi* in congealed mass,
Ever wield the halberd-axe,
Hand grasping the might of Celestial Soldiers—
At a single cry, gazing eyes shatter, hearts tremble.
Numinous Lords, Inspectors, and Listeners,
Hearken to the search, follow the sound.
The Nine Provinces’ Earth Deities,
Each summoned by name—
Execute and eradicate the fierce and wicked,
Those who incur guilt shall not lightly escape,
The wicked shall die, the kind shall live.
Sever heads, sever feet,
Pound and shatter their forms.
Ghosts and demons swept away,
The human realm rests in peace.
Where the talisman for curing illness and driving away evil arrives,
Enact it with divine might.
*Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!*

**Celestial Rigor Talisman**
The **Celestial Rigor Great Sage Talisman** wards off disasters for the state.
When sun and moon lose their measure,
When comets appear by day,
When drought, flood, locusts, or plague rage fiercely,
When malevolent ghosts and spirits invade the realm,
Manifesting hideous and monstrous forms,
Entering homes,
Hurling bricks and tiles,
Summoning winds to set fires,
Bewildering the living—
Inscribe the true form of the **Celestial Rigor Great Sage Talisman**,
Visualize the *qi* of the Breaker Star,
And, following the method, take and inscribe it.
For all the aforementioned matters,
When inscribing this talisman, proceed thus:
On the eve, prepare incense, flowers, wine, and fruit,
To offer to the Celestial Rigor Great Sage.
Set out paper, brush, and ink before the incense altar.
At dawn, banish all extraneous thoughts,
Purify body and mind,
And inscribe the talisman in accordance with the method.
The rest follow likewise.

**Conjoined Forms**
Method of Dispatching Talismans

The True Form of Zhenwu on the right,
Shields the body, secures the home,
Drives away and subdues demonic spirits and malevolent forces,
Dissolves grudges and curses,
Cures pestilence and suppresses lingering corpse-ghost afflictions.
Preserve and transcribe it with transformative script,
Visualize the talisman’s envoy:
Hair unbound, barefoot,
Clad in black,
Riding a black cloud,
With the Twenty-Eight Constellations in attendance.
The incantation reads:

*Envoy of the Dark Warrior, greatly display your numinous power.
Relieve the people’s suffering, sever all perverse essences.
Hunt and seize calamities, eradicate their forms.
Gather the soul to the body, settle the seven po.
Shield the body and dispel misfortune, eternally preserve longevity.
All spirits stand in awe—
Upon this decree, obey and act swiftly!
Hastily, as the statutes command!*

Next, employ the Thunder Bureau to dispatch the talisman,
Flash the eyes thrice,
Envision it as radiant lightning,
A thunderbolt shattering the patient’s dwelling,
Transforming it into a divine abode—
Golden steps, jade halls,
All within become immortals,
No trace of the mundane remains.

**Method for Crafting and Consecrating the Seal**
Formerly transmitted by the Perfected Master:
The seals of the Northern Culmen Demon-Dispelling Court and the Universal Great Dharma Lord—two faces—
May be carved from jujube wood struck by thunder.
On a day of the Six Ding or Six Jia, with utmost sincerity,
Burn incense, fast, and purify.
Command the artisan to carve them.
Then, on a jiazi night, when stars and moon shine brightly,
Beneath the canopy, prepare twenty-four cups of jujube broth,
Twenty-four platters of seasonal fruits,
Tea, wine, and incense.
First submit a memorial for approval,
Then present paper money and horses,
Offering them to the Dharma Lord of the Demon-Dispelling Court,
The seal-entering sacred assembly,
Heavenly Ding and Valiant Warriors,
Envoys of the Five Thunders,
Wind Earl and Rain Master,
Six Ding and Six Jia,
Flying talisman and swift-seal officers,
Seal-monitoring and seal-guarding deities,
Seal-bearing youths,
And the sacred hosts within the seal.

**Seal Designs**
*Northern Culmen Demon-Dispelling Court Seal*
*Universal Great Dharma Lord Seal*
Each seal of the Demon-Dispelling Court and the Universal Great Dharma Lord measures one cun and eight fen per side,
Forged from gold or jade,
Or carved from thunder-struck jujube wood.
Summon the envoys of the Six Ding and Six Jia to establish a boundary and stand guard.
Once placed, apply red cinnabar to the seal’s face.
First memorialize Heaven,
Then report to the Eastern Peak and all relevant authorities,
Ensuring reverent verification before use.

**Seal-Activating Incantation**
Recite before consecrating or using the seal:
*Divine seal of the Northern Culmen,
Worn with true numinosity.
The Three Masters descend,
Complying with my command.
With one press of the sacred seal,
Fortune and longevity arrive.
Malevolent forces submit to rectitude,
The Dao’s qi endures forever.
Hastily, as the statutes command!*

**Seal-Opening Incantation**
*Heavenly seal, numinous and bright,
By the Jade Emperor’s decree, dispel evil.
The Dharma Lord oversees, the seal,
Heavenly Ding and Valiant Warriors bear it forth.
Hearing this, perverse ways shatter in terror;
The afflicted, upon seeing it, find peace.
Those who bring calamity perish,
Those who act with kindness prosper.
Hastily, as the statutes command!*

**Seal-Using Incantation**
*Heavenly Emperor’s divine seal:
Seal a mountain—it becomes a lake,
Seal behind—it becomes a road,
Seal a tree—it withers,
Seal the earth—it splits,
Seal wood—its roots break,
Seal water—it ceases to flow.
Seal above—it pierces below,
Seal without—it penetrates within,
Seal before—it pierces behind,
Seal left—it pierces right,
Seal evil—evil halts,
Seal ghosts—ghosts vanish,
Seal illness—illness departs,
Seal pain—pain scatters.
Shatter demonic qi,
Dissolve ancestral misfortunes.
Hastily flee!
Righteous spirits, come and dwell in my place.
Hastily, as the statutes command!*

**Seal-Entering Incantation**
*Heavenly Ding and Valiant Warriors enter the heavenly seal,
Fiercely rend malevolent forces to dust.
Hastily, as the statutes command!*

**Ink-Combining Method**

**Fine Ink Preparation**
Two ounces of fine ink, one *fen* each of cinnabar, peach oil, willow oil, and toon oil soot—boil with a small measure of clear wine. Knead with soapberry seed glue. Prepare on the fifth day of the fifth month at noon.

*Incantation:*
Six Jia and Six Ding, divine ink most numinous.
Five Elders’ true *qi*, born of the Northern Transformation.
Mystic origin of the Dao’s root, slaying and beheading demonic essences.
Human spirits purified, ghosts and demons obliterated in form.
Dispatch talismans and memorials—obey the command and swiftly act.
*Hastily, as the statutes command!*

**Inkstone Water Blessing**
The Four Great Ones illuminate, Heaven and Earth endure.
Three Luminaries’ divine water dispels misfortune.
Inscribe talismans to slay ghosts, subdue [missing characters] beneath me.
Twin Stars guard, Seven Spirits radiate light.
Malevolent spirits cower, myriad *qi* harmonize in peace.
*Hastily, as the statutes command!*

**Vermilion Ink Brush Incantation**
The sun’s light shines everywhere—yin ghosts must wane.
Divine cinnabar brightens the eyes, its radiance reveals the Grand Tenuity.
What I now transform crushes all demons.
Seven *qi* form the Dipper, three *qi* form the Terrace.
Three Stars shine together—where the talisman arrives, swiftly pursue.
The brush is a divine sword, the ink a halberd.
By brushwork, cure illness—all evil subdued.
*Hastily, as the statutes command!*

Draw the sun’s *qi* into your mouth, recite the incantation, and visualize. Then grind the ink.

**Ink-Grinding Method**
First grind right forty-nine turns, reciting the twelve earthly branches, twenty-eight lunar lodges, sun and moon, *Tanlang* to *Pojun*.
Next grind left seven turns, reciting [missing characters].
When finished, gather the true *qi* of each star and blow it into the inkstone.

**Brush Collection and Offering Ritual**
On days of Six Ding and Six Jia, or the fifth day of the fifth month, bind twelve brushes, each seven *cun* and one *fen* long, using three tufts of purple bristles to correspond to the Three Terraces.
On a *jiazi* day at night when stars and moon are clear, bathe, change clothes, and perform the ritual while burning incense.
Present memorials and offerings to the Heavenly Rigid Great Sage, with spirit money and horses directed toward the Canopy of Flowers. Offer twelve cups of wax tea, form the Master’s mudra, and visualize Six Ding and Six Jia emerging from the Heavenly Gate, descending on black clouds to transform the brushes into the divine generals of Six Jia and Six Ding.

*Incantation:*
Heavenly Ding and Valiant Warriors, Six Jia and Six Ding.
Wise and upright, wielding evil with utmost efficacy.
Demons fear, malevolent ghosts tremble.
Aid Heaven’s transformations, sweeping away demonic essences.
Assist my Daoist arts, deliver and protect all beings.
Command the divine brush to swiftly descend with might.
Inscribe talismans to slay ghosts, obliterate traces and forms.
By the Emperor’s decree, *hastily obey!*

**Water Collection and Offering Ritual**
First use the Master’s mudra, then the Emperor’s mudra—employ both incantations together.
On days of Heavenly Virtue, Monthly Virtue, Six Jia and Six Ding, or when the King of Vajra descends, collect rainwater in a bottle. Each month, on the Canopy of Flowers, face the Heavenly Rigid Great Sage, Heavenly Virtue, Monthly Virtue, and the Five Emperor Dragon Lords to perform the offering.
Purify the heart and maintain ritual purity. Visualize the sagely host descending from the Heavenly Gate on black clouds, transforming into the water. Use the Master’s mudra.
Offer twelve cups of scalding tea and spirit money, then burn them after reciting the incantation.
First transform one portion for the Earth God, then for Ding and Jia. Offer spirit money and horses for the brushes in the same manner.

*Incantation:*
Heavenly Virtue and Monthly Virtue, Five Emperor Dragon Lords.
Heaven’s regulators, honored stars of *Pojun*.
Commanding divine generals, Six Jia and Six Ding.
Peerless in spiritual power, fiercest in might.
Bestow divine water to deliver all beings.
Inscribe talismans and registers to capture and slay demonic essences.
Cure illness and expel afflictions, utterly eradicating their forms.
*Hastily, as the statutes command!*

**Spirit Money Transformation Incantation**
Transform the spirit into the Master, right hand forming the sword mudra.
By the formless Dharma-symbol, fire is the means.
Burn and transform the spirit money;
Clouds of incense rise in fragrance.
Only pray the divine immortals bestow grace and blessings.
On the third recitation: *Great Dao divine immortals, bestow grace and blessings.*
Arrange the spirit money and horses in order and burn them together.

*On behalf of [so-and-so] for [such-and-such] matter, I rely upon the incense-bearing Merit Clerk to transmit this petition directly to the Supreme Emperor, beseeching the descent of the Dipper’s Rigid True *Qi* to empower my brushwork, expel evil, uphold rectitude, and unite with the Dao in truth.*

*Divine brush, divine and numinous,
In union with the spirits it aligns.

**Method to Halt a Child’s Night Crying**

Take a small fire and burn the end of a stick of firewood, six inches in length, sharpening its tip. Scrape away the charred bark where burned, face south to transform into spirit, and make the mudra of your original master. Draw in the true qi of the Southern Fire Star, inhale one breath into your mouth, and blow it onto the tip of the stick. Inhale again and hold the breath, then inscribe the following twenty characters upon it. Place it beneath the bed, driving it into the moon’s broken phase. Take care to avoid disturbance.

*I possess a fire-stirring rod,
Which I appoint as gatekeeper.
Seizing the night-crying ghost,
I shall not release it till dawn.*

There is a talisman—transmitted orally and imprinted upon the heart.

**Method to Halt Headaches**
Use the Three Lights Talisman and affix it to the temples. Then draw in the qi of Heavenly Rigor, exhaling upon it three times. The pain will immediately cease.

**Method to Dispel Swelling Toxins**
Make the Dipper Mudra and silently recite the Three Lights Incantation seven times. Draw in the qi of the Three Lights and exhale upon it three times. The swelling will naturally disperse. The same applies to injuries from poisonous snakes or creatures.

**Method to Treat Red Eyes**
First transform into spirit and make the mudra of your original master. Draw in the qi of the Two Lights and infuse it into water. Then shout once, make the Dipper Mudra, and recite the incantation:

*Oṃ vajra riyaye □ḍa,
You are Li Gongzhong,
Why have you come to my home?
Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!*

Recite it three times, shout three times, and use the water to rinse the eyes.

**Method to Suppress Malaria**
First transform into the Star Officials Zhang and Yi—each a hundred feet tall, clad in green cloud-scarves, wielding jade tablets, dwelling in the south, and governing malaria ghosts. The ancestral name of the malaria ghost resembles that of the Black Grief ghost. Use the Dipper Mudra to write these six characters on paper money, then brush the patient three times before burning it outside the door. Visualize the petitioner as the Day Officer of Divine Merit for that day, face north to burn incense, and rewrite the names of the seven stars of the Dipper, having the patient swallow them. The illness will immediately cease. Also write the character "general" and bind it to the patient’s left middle finger for males or right for females. The master should press the character "flower" onto the talisman. Once the malaria ceases, burn the talisman with paper money outside the door. Boiling peach branches into a decoction and adding the Three Lights Talisman is especially effective. Visualize the Star Officials Zhang and Yi capturing and severing the ancestral name of the malaria ghost, which resembles the Black Grief ghost. Recite the incantation fourteen times.

**Childbirth-Hastening Talisman (Also Effective Against Rats)**
Take a cypress stick four inches long and three fingers wide. Place a brush at the Heavenly Gate, burn incense toward the broken phase, then stand with both feet together, first opening the front (called "Opening the Heavenly Gate") and then the back (called "Closing the Earthly Door"). Sit at the Xun position, facing Qian, and make the Mudras of the Pleiades and the Sun. Visualize yourself within the mouth of the Northern Dipper, drawing the true purple qi of the Star Giant Gate and channeling it down to infuse the brush. With one breath, inscribe the talisman. Hang it within the birthing chamber, but ensure the pregnant woman does not see it before labor, lest it disturb the fetus.

**Talisman Design:**
For hastening childbirth, inscribe the talisman on a three-inch square of paper. Visualize the Four Commanders of the Four Directions—clenched fists, heads bound with black cloth, wearing crimson robes with wide sleeves—arraying demon-quelling thunder, lightning, and fire chariots. Bite down on the talisman, silently recite the incantation seven times:

*Heaven and Earth unite,
Sun and Moon unite,
Human and ghost unite.*

Recite this once with a single breath. Then visualize the talisman’s soldiers—thunder, lightning, and fire chariots—entering the abdomen with the talisman. Swallow it with freshly drawn water. For males, hold it in the left hand; for females, the right, and expel it from the hand.

**Master Xu’s Incantation for Water to Treat Illness**
*Southern Celestial Pivot,
Northern Dark Warrior,
Eastern Old Lord,
Western White Tiger,
Heavenly Elder,
Earthly Matriarch.
Divine water of the Five Directions,
Descend and manifest your register!*

First recite the incantation ten thousand times; thereafter, seven times suffice. For all incantations, first make the Thunder Duke’s Mudra and recite it twenty-one times in one breath. Draw in the qi of the Five Directions and Heavenly Rigor, infusing it into the water. This method may be applied to all illnesses, yielding great merit. Using it alongside the Three Lights Talisman is especially efficacious.

**Thunder Duke’s Mudra**
Raise the left hand, clasp the right. Hook the left hand’s fourth finger around the right hand’s third finger. Press the right hand’s second finger onto the left hand’s fourth finger. Hook the left hand’s third finger around the right hand’s fourth finger. Press the back of the left hand’s fifth finger against the back of the right hand’s fourth finger at the middle joint. Hook the right hand’s fifth finger around the left hand’s fifth finger. The left thumb presses the middle joint of the left hand’s second finger, while the right thumb presses the Zi character.

*Thus concludes the second scroll of* The Supreme Essential Secrets for Assisting the State and Saving the People.
*Here begins the third scroll of* The Supreme Essential Secrets for Assisting the State and Saving the People.

Master Dongyou’s Yuanmiao Zong Compilation:
*Talismanic Methods for Dispelling Consumptive Wasting and All Diseases, Together with the Authentic Rites of Tianpeng for Beheading Demons*

**On the Treatment of Consumptive Wasting**

The affliction of corpse-worms and transmitted ailments arises from the treatment of illness yet originates in indulgent desires. When indulgent desires remain unchecked, they lead to untimely demise. Though death may come early, if the celestial allotment of years has not yet expired, such deaths are deemed unjustly premature. Since the underworld has not yet summoned or constrained them, nor have they undergone karmic retribution, their ethereal souls linger in stagnation, unable to attain liberation. Thus, they transform into yin-demonic qi, infecting their kin through the bones. In most cases, they seek nothing more than to depend upon and draw from the qi of the living.

These worms consume a person’s essence and blood until emaciation sets in, spreading through the five viscera and causing unceasing convulsions. Often, entire clans are brought to ruin by this, a grievous sorrow indeed. In severe cases, neither medicinal remedies nor acupuncture can cure it. Even if Sangong were alive today or Hua Tuo reborn, how could they restore such patients?

Alas, the people suffer innocently, unjustly drowned in calamity. Moved by compassion, Heaven has revealed the Daoist methods. As the scriptures state: *"If the illness has not yet advanced deeply, and the joints remain unbreached, it may still be treated. But if the joints have already been passed, attempts at healing will prove futile. However, by applying this method, future afflictions may be averted."*

For those seeking deliverance, the afflicted household must provide a detailed written account, describing the patient’s initial onset of illness—its time, place, and cause—as well as any encounters with the deceased appearing in dreams, or connections to malevolent ghosts and demonic entities.

In performing these rites, sincerity and reverence are paramount. All ritual offerings, sacred gifts, and invocations of qi should be prepared according to one’s means, whether modest or generous. For impoverished households, the officiating master may provide the necessary items. Wealthier families should adhere to the prescribed rites and prepare the proper jiao offerings to repay Heaven’s grace.

The officiating master must guard against greed, never diverting ritual offerings for personal use. All received items should be dedicated to incense, scripture recitations, and the maintenance of sacred fires. Secondly, they should aid reclusive ascetics in the mountains and the destitute in the world. While adhering to proper protocols, one must not begrudge wealth or treat sacred arts with contempt, lest one profane the august sages and incur divine censure. The statutes are clear—this is a matter to be approached with utmost caution.

Below are the proven talismans, recorded in full:

**Talisman for Severing Corpse-Infestation (to be ingested daily, with all forms of the talisman gathered in one scroll, written in cinnabar)**

**Talisman for Slaying Transmitted-Wasting Worms and Annihilating Corpse-Demons**
Once the talisman is drawn, place it in a clean, plain vessel filled with pure water, setting it before the patient. Have another person hold the talisman and drop it into the water without disturbing it. If the talisman sinks within seven days, the wasting demons and corpse-worms will perish, and the illness will be instantly cured. If the talisman floats, recovery from the wasting disease will be delayed. This method is divinely efficacious and must not be transmitted to unworthy recipients.

**Supreme Purple Court Talisman**

Whenever inscribing the Supreme Purple Court Talisman, first burn incense and pace the Dipper’s steps. Clearly articulate the affliction at hand, then visualize the Five True Lords of the Five Directions—Metal, Wood, Water, Fire, and Earth—standing before the writing surface, each emanating radiance that transforms *qi* into the inkstone. The inkstone becomes a Black Dragon Pool, the ink a forest of halberds, the brush a divine sword. Then grind the ink forty-nine turns to the left while silently reciting the Heavenly Penetrating Spirit Incantation, exhaling *qi* into the inkstone. Next, grind forty-nine turns to the right, silently invoking the Twenty-Eight Constellations, the Twelve Monthly Generals, the names of the Seven Stars, and the Spirit Lords of the Eight Trigrams, exhaling *qi* into the inkstone. Then envision the inkstone’s brilliance outshining the sun.

Thereafter, form the Jade Emperor’s mudra and recite the brush incantation:
*"Heaven is round, earth is square,
Six pitch-pipes, nine chapters.
With one stroke of this divine brush,
Ten thousand demons vanish.*
*Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!"*

After reciting the incantation, tap the brush three times or draw three strokes upon the writing surface. When inscribing the talisman, if the day is yin, do so by daylight; if yang, by night. Disperse the form.

A single *qi* blends into oneness, the Two Modes harmonize in peace.
One: Earth. Two: Water. Three: Fire. Four: Metal. Five: Wood.
The heavens are round—begin the stroke at the Gate of Heaven.
The earth is square—begin the stroke at the Earthly Portal.
*Leihuo, Leihuo.*
The Six *Ding* spirits dwell on the left; the White Tiger’s might stands beside.
The Heavenly *Ding* warriors sever demons and inauspiciousness.
Mountain spirits, revenants, and transmitted afflictions vanish.

Turn the *Leihuo* twice—Heaven and Earth brighten.
Three turns—the Three Generals assist.
Four turns—the Four Sages aid.
Five turns—the Five Prisons lend strength.
Six turns—ten thousand illnesses perish.
Seven turns—the Seven Stars support.
Eight turns—the Eight Directions are subdued.
By the decree of the Jade Emperor, the Highest Lord of Heaven—*Gather the form.*

Write this talisman on a separate sheet of paper as before.
**First, to sever transmitted afflictions:** Swallow the talisman after burning it in one place.
If desiring to ingest it, first sweep and purify a clean chamber. Place a lamp to the left for men, to the right for women, with half a cup of oil prepared. At the still of night, thread the talisman onto a needle, burn it to ash, and in a clean bowl, burn incense. Invoke the patient’s surname, birth month, age, the cause of their suffering, and the true sages of the talisman. Then mix the talisman ash with ritual water and consume it. Have the patient sit facing their life-direction, silent. One or two attendants should remain. Soon, the sufferer may seem to dream of ghosts departing—ask their names. Or if they see insects emerging from their body, swiftly seize the insects, fry them in the oil, and cast them into flowing water to forever sever transmission.

**Incantation for Water to Treat Consumptive Illnesses and Miscellaneous Ailments (Universally Applicable):**
*"Water of the Great One, primordial and fine,
Raise it to the mouth, divine radiance flows.
From the large intestine, trickling to the bladder,
It scours the five viscera, entering the womb.
A hundred illnesses heal, evil spirits flee,
Aligning with Heaven and Earth, the body light and strong.
Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!"*

Face the sun when reciting the incantation over the water by day, or gaze toward the Morning Star by night, silently repeating it seven times. Draw in qi and blow it into the water, then use it to harmonize talismans for expelling worms. After the patient’s worms emerge, they must consume the Talismans of the Three Lights and Five Thunders each morning and evening to purge accumulated malign matter from the five viscera. After a month, full recovery will follow—provided they perpetually abstain from anger, excessive desires, and all raw, oily, or greasy foods. This method is especially efficacious.

**Five-Thunder Spirit Talismans**
In former years, your servant Miaozong received these Five-Thunder Talismans from a master and has employed them for over twenty years. They have cured critical illnesses, women’s ghostly pregnancies and ghostly qi, abdominal masses, transverse or stillborn fetuses, and all manner of demonic afflictions, saving countless sufferers from distress. Now, by the grace of the Sagely Emperor and the esoteric methods of the Dao, I dare not conceal them. I have meticulously compiled them here for transmission to later disciples—guard them well.

When ingesting the talisman, decoct seven peach leaves or seven peach kernels, face south, and swallow five pellets. All malign matter from the five viscera will be purged.

**Great Fire Bell Talisman**
**Dispersed Form**

Eastward Waving the Great Fire, Westward Crossing the *Yeni* Fire, Seal the Door of Earth, Secure the Human Gate, Block the Ghostly Path, Northern *Yudan* Void Fire, Southern *Danyan* Blazing Fire, Green Fire to the South, Red Fire to the West, White Fire to the North, Black Fire to the North, Yellow Fire at the Center, Twelve *Shen*, Eighteen Lunar Mansion Fires, Northern Culmen Great Emperor, Seven Primal Star Lords Leading Heavenly Soldiers, Five-Thunder Troops, Six Regulators of Ghosts and Demons, Great Fire.

**Assembled Form**

For inscribing the Great Fire Bell Talisman, first perform the rites as before, pace the Net of the Seven Stars, form the Jade Emperor’s Mudra, and visualize the great fires of each direction blazing fiercely, descending to infuse the cinnabar brush and inkstone. Once the talisman is complete, place it where the anomaly occurs to suppress it; efficacy will be immediate.

**Iron Fan Talisman**

Set the intention as if beholding the sun, grasp the Gongcao Seal with the left hand, and pace the Qian Yuan Net. Then, visualize the writing desk as an altar, the paper as silk, the ink as a hundred medicines, and the brush as a sharp blade. Draw the true *qi* of each of the Seven Stars of the Northern Dipper, blow it into the inkstone, then grind the ink: twelve turns to the left, invoking the Twelve Monthly Generals; twelve turns to the right, invoking the Twelve Hourly Spirits—twenty-four turns in all, corresponding to the Twenty-Four *Qi*. Consecrate the brush and inscribe the talisman, reciting the incantation:

Heaven is round, Earth is square,
Six Pitches, Nine Chapters.
With one stroke of the divine brush,
Ten thousand ghosts perish.
Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by statute and ordinance.

When inscribing the talisman with the incantation, envision the recipient as the Child Hastening Birth. As you dispatch the talisman, observe the person receiving it, using left or right hand to discern the child’s sex. If the talisman is to be swallowed, use flowing water while facing north. When dispatching the talisman, employ the Thunder Duke Mudra.

**Fire Wheel Talisman**

Toward the sun, inscribe one fire character with the Golden Spear, reciting the True Sovereign of Fiery Virtue and Blazing Deluder of the Southern Direction. Inscribe another fire character, reciting the All-Responsive True Sovereign of the Red Emperor. Inscribe yet another fire character, then recite the Three True Sovereigns once more. Draw three streams of solar fire qi through the nose into the heart.
